the wildest thing is that, individually, a lot of that morning routine isnt bad practice. your brain does sort stuff out while you sleep, but not *every* dream is important, remembering to remember them is a fine skill to build tho. i used to take cold showers when i had to wake up at 4:30AM in highschool cause it slapped me awake, but it isnt always necessary. doing puzzles periodically does help with mundane small tasks, but doing them daily only does so much for "strengthening" your brain. daily meditation is also good for sorting out your thoughts, but takes routine practice to be able to use effectively for that purpose. fixing your bed every day can be part of a morning meditation! its a mindful small task that takes less than 10 minutes and requires a lot of full body movements to complete. having a todo list each day even if small is a routine i picked up as someone with DID and ADHD who gets off track and unable to remember what track i was on throughout the day. doing these things isnt gonna make you a billionaire, it just makes being alive a bit nicer if done as your ability to do so allows you.

Dream explanation  1. You feel like you dont have enough time to do what you want and what gives you happiness, because youre always on the next item. Even though you enjoy what you do, you have the nagging feeling whether youre doing what you want or what you feel you need to do (is your work life in balance?)  1a? You pissing on the bed signifies your reluctance at the status quo. You dont want to follow the rules and take your dreams as an ability to do whatever your free will allows, no matter how absurd. its not about the piss, its about your ability to piss wherever you want. In other words, its your subconscious telling you "No, I do what i want! and if i want to piss, thats my choice!"  2. Even though you like the job you do, it still feels like working in the service industry. Even though you ignore the hateful comments, the sense of entitlement from the customers (audience) gets to you. Comments pushing you do a certain style (or frequency) and then still complaining makes you equate it to working at the service industry and having customers constantly complain.  3, You feel like leaving everything behind, starting over. You want to test yourself and understand if your position is luck or your own hard work.  4. Its strange how You brought alcohol, and You got in trouble. Its never someone else, and youre there. its you. A overexaggerated sense of self importance, i guess. Might mean you feel like your ego is going unchecked, and that sooner or later youll be called out on it?  5.  You feel the need to connect, and have just thought of the name because you heard it and subconsciously thought what would person X be like in real life. it could mean 2 things: - your desire to form meaningful relationships offline, a feeling that youre overdependent on your online persona - a desire to show that you are tolerant enough to hang out with anyone, no matter how obscure they are. its a reflection of self doubt and a check on your own ego    Your dreams show that youre still very unconfident in the type of work you produce. Even though you like it and enjoy making it, you still feel a lot of pressure to perform a certain way. However, being rebellious at heart you constantly consciously or subconsciously search for ways to fight any routine in your life.

15:15 Cold showers are super relaxing. For me initially before I started cold showers I would stay like 30mins to an hour every time I take a bath, I would take so long because I would get lost in my thoughts. It got to the point where I would tell my family "hey, I'll help you out with that thing after I take this short shower" and they would reply "nevermind, I need help now not in an hour" and just like when the MacDonald's clerk started to recognize and give me "the usual" I knew it was time for change.  So I started doing cold showers, immediately I could see the benefits instead of taking like an hour I would finish in 3 mins because "f*ck this, god it's painful". A problem started to arise though, I would dread taking a bath instead of taking a bath for 30mins I would spend about 30mins in the bath trying to psyche myself up to enter the bath.  So I started to modify the cold shower a bit. I would have warm water at the start and then when I am already in the shower I would drop the temp and end it with a cold rinse. Suddenly it was starting to click and my body was able to adjust to the cold and gradually improve.  I think to get the best benefit out of cold showers you need to truly understand them, cold showers wake up the body and relax muscles. A cold shower after an intensive exercise is bliss. People also need to stop villainizing hot showers, hot showers make the body sleepy and similarly relax muscles they're best before bed. You can also mix and match showers within one bath, 1 minute very hot, 1 minute very cold there's alot of variations.  Most importantly cold showers finally allowed my lizard body to adjust to the cold. My country's temperature casually goes to 70C (160F for the freedom warriors) so I was fully adjusted to the hot temperature, but when the temperature drops to 5C (40F) I would act like a lil-bitch. Now cold showers have allowed me to evolve to be able to resist scalding heat and freezing cold, I am invincible now
14:22 Mediation is a skill that you practice, I used to get bored in the 3 min mark then after a while I was able to meditate for 10 minutes. Then I got lazy and stopped meditating and now I reach 6-7 minutes. Honestly meditating is really helpful, you don't have to do like 20-30mins even 5mins to calm down your nerves, reset your focus and allow you to re-prioritize your goals is very useful. Especially for a person with ADHD

Hey Kurtis, this video is absolutely hilarious and I understand your point. These billionaires don't truly understand the struggle of the working class and I think the concept of a billionaire shouldn't even fucking exist.. However, some of what he does in this routine is stuff I've learned in therapy. He comes off as pretentious but I wouldn't discount everything he is saying. And you don't need to do every one of these every day; just picking one or two could help someone.  --Rituals and routines are important for mental stability--people with ADHD or ASD often love having routines or rituals. Decision fatigue is a literal psychological concept, and if you have a routine, you really don't have to think too much and make too many decisions.  --Recalling your dreams is pretentious but only if you're rich.  --Making your bed can help maintain some sense of order, even if you don't have the energy to do anything else. --Vitamins and probiotics are good for you but not necessary to human survival and can be expensive so L on that one. --It is SO cringe that they refer to this breathing technique as alpha breathing (also the tongue thing is weird), but I've practiced 4-8-7 breathing sans creepy smile/tongue dance on many occasions for my anxiety. It slows my heart rate and makes me feel more grounded. Breathing techniques, again, are widely encouraged (again no source but therapy patient).  --Meditation, again, a great coping mechanism to try. --1-2 minutes of just movement is a fantastic concept. It doesn't have to be insane/you don't have to exert yourself, but getting the blood flowing and stretching out your muscles after sleep can't hurt. --Cold shower? Psychopath. /j --Tea? Whatever, but honestly better than coffee. I wouldn't wish a caffeine addiction on anyone. I have a huge addiction to caffeine. --Journaling is a widely encouraged coping mechanism amongst psychologists (I don't have sources for this other from my experiences with different therapists). --To-do list of three things? If you interpret that a different way, he could be saying those are just his goals for the day and he would like to reach them throughout his day. Not that once he does all 3 things he stops doing anything. Having a small list of things may help someone create good habits without overloading them. For me, personally, I could think of call dentist to schedule appointment, read chapter 1 of my textbook, and take my meds. Small goals can be huge ones for some people. --"A lot of who we are is our states and emotions" is awesome. For someone with a mood disorder as well as anxiety/ADHD, a lot of my life has been ruled by my emotions and I let my emotions take over me. A "to-feel" list could be feasible, but not always. If you know watching puppy videos will make you a little happy, then there. Number one is to feel happy by watching puppy videos.  --Boo on the human doings. --Reading? Great habit! --Smoothies aren't a bad option but not all of those fresh foods are accessible to everyone. --Website courses bullshit.   I am aware not everyone is able bodied and not everyone has 18 hours to live out their mornings, however doing just one of these things could improve someone's mental health. What's interesting, however, is how these ideas are geared towards men--we don't refer to any of this as therapeutic, it has to be tough guy macho man shit. Why? Why do we have to smother these legitimate coping skills in testosterone in order to appeal to men? Society has taught us that men are supposed to be tough, without emotion. Maybe this is the only way to get through to them?  I'm probably overanalyzing but a lot of what he said I have learned in therapy. Sharing these techniques in a more digestible way could help someone here.

Excellent video! I think you're spot on when you called it â€œhustle-mindset propagandaâ€. Small changes built up over time can improve your life, but these billionaires were born wealthy and made money off the backs of others, you won't become one by making your bed and drinking smoothies. I'm not a billionaire, I guess being disabled I'm kind of the opposite of one?? But because of this I've had the time and the need to try a lot of the stuff on this list. Here are my thoughts.  -Make bed...I'm in my mid 30s and I only make my bed if company is coming. No one cares, do it if you want but it's not that important. Especially if you share a bed with someone who isn't awake yet. It's more important to do a few chores around the house, like starting some laundry or cleaning up in the kitchen. Your morning routine of taking the dog out is actually already a good habit.  -Drinking water is important, and especially if you take morning medications. Some meds don't work as well or can make you nauseous without a full glass of water. If you don't drink enough water it can be helpful to set aside time, but I found it more useful to replace other beverages with water. I almost never drink soda or coffee anymore. It's a bummer at first but it will feel better later. I noticed eating breakfast isn't on the list, I guess the smoothie is supposed to replace your morning meal, but the ingredients listed are...ugh. It's easier and tastes better to grab a bunch of frozen bags of mixed fruits and vegetables (you can find them specifically for smoothies), and blend it with ice. I like to add protein powder (I prefer vanilla), chia seeds, ginger and lecithin. Juice or water to help it blend. But if you're hungry you should eat. Find some healthy things that you like eating. You need energy for the rest of the day!   -Here's a tip: Breathing, meditating, and moving your body should be done at roughly the same time! Just pick a yoga video on youtube, there's tons of them. Yoga with Adrienne and Yoga with Kassandra are both great. Breathe while you move. Meditate in shavasana. Breathe while you meditate! Focusing on the breath is a tried and true meditation technique. And yes, boredom is normal. Strong feelings seemingly out of nowhere can be normal. It will pass, especially when you start learning more about how meditation works. I recommend the apps waking up and medito. And lumenate if you want to try something kind of weird. It helps me with migraines.  -I can't take cold showers because I get hives, but a quick shower can wake you up, and you can use hot and cold water to regulate emotions, cold for anxiety, warm for depression. But honestly, if you don't like cold showers you can just splash cold water on your face and get the same effect faster and more comfortably. The key with a lot of this stuff is to create long term habits, so you should start small and not burden yourself with lots of things you aren't enjoying.  -Tea has been one of the most helpful things I've found personally. Mint helps with digestion, ginger with pain, chamomile and valerian for relaxation and sleep, green (I use jasmine) for energy. There's no reason you have to do this in the morning. Just do it as needed. You're already chugging water and smoothies, I would say tea might be better later in the day, or even before bed, or of course as needed to help with pain, anxiety, etc. I got a nice Uncle Iroh tea pot and a warmer with a tea light candle in it and I just keep it in my office and drink it while I work.  -Journaling, reading, dream recall, brain training AND list making??? That's so much! I don't exactly journal because I already do a lot of writing. I do log my meals, take down my blood pressure, and make to-do and grocery lists. I would say it's good to have a journal if you feel like there's something you want to write down, for example if you have a dream you think is significant. Dream recall is mostly just useful if you have a lot of nightmares you want to work through, or if you want to learn lucid dreaming. But if your dreams don't concern you, there's no need to re-visit them. I would say focus on sleep hygiene instead. My entire life (including my dreams) improved when I started CPAP for sleep apnea, and sleep medications to help me fall asleep and stay asleep (but I haven't needed them since starting CPAP). Focus on trying to go to sleep and wake up at roughly the same time each day. Reading is great, but there's no need to do it in the morning unless that's the best time you have to set aside. The â€œto-feel and â€œto-beâ€ lists are a strange thing to do every day, in my opinion. I make these kinds of lists every few months, or when I'm feeling stuck, stagnant or displeased with my life. Usually the lists I make are more like â€œwho am Iâ€ and â€œwhat do I want/needâ€. In my experience, seeing a therapist regularly is better than all this. A good therapist can help you organize your thoughts and help you figure out how to achieve your goals, and if you have a more significant problem in life, having a therapist who already knows you can really help. I've been seeing my current therapist bi-weekly for six years and she's amazing. She got me through some really dark times, and is helping me become the person I want to be in spite of my limitations.

Actually controlling your emotions is possible. After attending DBT for 3 years (twice a week for half a year, once a week the rest) I was able to better recognize emotions (as well as distinguish anxiety from gut feelings), prevent panic attacks by recognizing them ahead of time and doing skills to calm down and manage my emotions. I wanted to offer an alternative view on your sells. Although not the exact ones in the video, those were lame as fuck.  There are a few of your sells that I personally enjoy with modifications. For instance, good breathing techniques actually have a lot of benefits to them. My personal favorite is Wim Hof breathing, which when done properly will oxygenate your body to a point where it is like a mild high, and has lots of benefits for metabolism and energy. If you look up Wim Hof breathing he has a site that will give you the basic rundown, and I think it's good to do. He also uses it in conjunction with cold exposure and really cold showers as a way of boosting his cold resistance, which actually works. He was recorded sitting in a tub of ice for two hours without losing any body temperature, and also hiked MT. Kilimanjaro in his shorts in record time. Cold showers still suck though, but I do enjoy a cool shower in warmer seasons. Definitely not in winter though fuck that. Also, I'm personally a tea person and I try not to drink lots of caffeine, so I definitely vibe with the tea. Usually I'll do a green tea for a lower amount of caffeine, or yerba mate for a higher amount. I also enjoy journaling. I wouldn't do it every day because frankly my life isn't full enough to write about interesting things that often, but it's really nice to put your thoughts to paper periodically. I've noticed it's a healthy outlet for bottled up emotions. As for smoothies, the best ones are with high quality apple juice. I'm a Coloradoan, and we have Big B's apple cider here which makes, on my life the best smoothies out there. They also have a cold pressed version that is literally just juice squeezed from apples and bottled, no pasteurization. If you're in Colorado I definitely recommend. The regular juice is more common, but the cold pressed is only in stores from like September to December and only really at Whole Foods. Still worth a trip imo.

The "How to Feel" list seems nutty, but emotional intelligence research might actually support it.  Emotionally intelligent people identify what feelings would be helpful, and seek out those feelings.    For example, if something bad happens, you might feel discouraged.  Being discouraged might lead to giving up.  Emotionally intelligent people identify that feeling energized, flexible, or optimistic might be more helpful, and then they take action designed to help them feel that way, like listening to a motivational podcast, brainstorming options with a friend, or praying.  So you can't just flip a 'feelings' switch, but you can do things to help you get the feelings you want.  #mentalhealthnerd #thanksforcomingtomyTEDtalk

What's interesting about the first part is that he's right. (He's wrong about everything else though). Dreaming allows your brain to process emotions and things that happened during the day without GABA (gamma aminobutyric acid)- the neurotransmitter in your brain responsible for regulating anxiety. It allows your brain to process negative things logically without any extra fear.   This is why when you don't sleep well, you have a worse day than you would have if you got a good nights sleep. This is also why if you have a bad day, you often feel better the next morning.   Dreams don't actually mean anything, its just random shit your brain shows  you. Thats why they don't make sense.   Anyway, try to get enough sleep, it's very important!
